style="plainlist">\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eutardigrada" title="Eutardigrada">\n            Eutardigrada\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Heterotardigrada" title="Heterotardigrada">\n            Heterotardigrada\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Mesotardigrada" title="Mesotardigrada">\n            Mesotardigrada\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Tardigrades\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">\n            t\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90r/: \'ar\' in \'far\'">\n            \xc9\x91\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xa1/: \'g\' in \'guy\'">\n            \xc9\xa1\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">\n            r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ; also known colloquially as\n       <b>\n        water bears,\n       </b>\n       <b>\n        space bears,\n       </b>\n       or\n       <b>\n        moss piglets\n       </b>\n       )\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Scientist_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-American_Scientist-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRD-20140321_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WRD-20140321-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       are water-dwelling, eight-legged, segmented\n       <a href="/wiki/Micro-animal" title="Micro-animal">\n        micro-animals\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Scientist_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-American_Scientist-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They were first discovered by the German zoologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze" title="Johann August Ephraim Goeze">\n        Johann August Ephraim Goeze\n       </a>\n       in 1773. The name\n       <i>\n        <b>\n         Tardigrada\n        </b>\n       </i>\n       (meaning "slow stepper") was given three years later by the Italian biologist\n       <a href="/wiki/Lazzaro_Spallanzani" title="Lazzaro Spallanzani">\n        Lazzaro Spallanzani\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bordenstein_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bordenstein-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They have been found everywhere: from mountaintops to the deep sea and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mud_volcanoes" title="Mud volcanoes">\n        mud volcanoes\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       from tropical\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rain_forests" title="Rain forests">\n        rain forests\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">\n        Antarctic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades are one of the most resilient animals known.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP-20170714_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WP-20170714-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20170714_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAT-20170714-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Individual species of tardigrades can survive extreme conditions that would be rapidly fatal to nearly all other known life forms, including complete global mass\n       <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">\n        extinction events\n       </a>\n       due to\n       <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">\n        astrophysical events\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supernovae" title="Supernovae">\n        supernovae\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma-ray_bursts" title="Gamma-ray bursts">\n        gamma-ray bursts\n       </a>\n       , or large\n       <a href="/wiki/Impact_event" title="Impact event">\n        meteorite impacts\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP-20170714_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WP-20170714-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NAT-20170714_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NAT-20170714-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some tardigrades can withstand temperatures down to 1\xc2\xa0K (\xe2\x88\x92458\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F; \xe2\x88\x92272\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) (close to\n       <a href="/wiki/Absolute_zero" title="Absolute zero">\n        absolute zero\n       </a>\n       ) while others can withstand 420\xc2\xa0K (300\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F; 150\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       for several minutes, pressures about six times greater than those found in the deepest ocean trenches,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">\n        ionizing radiation\n       </a>\n       at doses hundreds of times higher than the lethal dose for a human, and the vacuum of outer space.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150907_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150907-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They can go without food or water for more than 30 years, drying out to the point where they are 3% or less water, only to rehydrate, forage, and reproduce.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRD-20140321_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WRD-20140321-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-auto-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guidetti.2C_R._.26_J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K.I._2002_181.E2.80.93187_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Guidetti.2C_R._.26_J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K.I._2002_181.E2.80.93187-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrades, living in harsh conditions, undergo an annual process of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cyclomorphosis" title="Cyclomorphosis">\n        cyclomorphosis\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="What changes does it undergo? (May 2017)">\n           further explanation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       They are not considered\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extremophilic" title="Extremophilic">\n        extremophilic\n       </a>\n       because they are not adapted to exploit these conditions. This means that their chances of dying increase the longer they are exposed to the extreme environments,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bordenstein_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bordenstein-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       whereas true\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">\n        extremophiles\n       </a>\n       thrive in a physically or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geochemical" title="Geochemical">\n        geochemically\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Extreme_environment" title="Extreme environment">\n        extreme environment\n       </a>\n       that would harm most other organisms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRD-20140321_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WRD-20140321-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Usually, tardigrades are about 0.5\xc2\xa0mm (0.02\xc2\xa0in; 19.69 thou) long when they are fully grown.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Scientist_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-American_Scientist-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They are short and plump with four pairs of legs, each with four to eight claws also known as "disks".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-American_Scientist_2-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-American_Scientist-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first three pairs of legs are directed ventrolaterally and are the primary means of locomotion, while the fourth pair is directed posteriorly on the terminal segment of the trunk and is used primarily for grasping the substrate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrades are prevalent in\n       <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">\n        mosses\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">\n        lichens\n       </a>\n       and feed on plant cells, algae, and small invertebrates. When collected, they may be viewed under a very low-power microscope, making them accessible to students and amateur scientists.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades form the\n       <a href="/wiki/Phylum" title="Phylum">\n        phylum\n       </a>\n       Tardigrada, part of the superphylum\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecdysozoa" title="Ecdysozoa">\n        Ecdysozoa\n       </a>\n       . It is an ancient group, with fossils dating from 530\xc2\xa0million years ago, in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">\n        Cambrian\n       </a>\n       period.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       About 1,150 species of tardigrades have been described.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zhang2011_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Zhang2011-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrades can be found throughout the world, from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">\n        Himalayas\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       (6,000 m; 20,000 ft, above sea level) to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_sea" title="Deep sea">\n        deep sea\n       </a>\n       (\xe2\x88\x924,000\xc2\xa0m; \xe2\x88\x9213,000\xc2\xa0ft) and from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_region" title="Polar region">\n        polar regions\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">\n        equator\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Description">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Description\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">\n         <a href="#Anatomy_and_morphology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Anatomy and morphology\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3">\n         <a href="#Reproduction">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Reproduction\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#Ecology_and_life_history">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Ecology and life history\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5">\n         <a href="#Physiology">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Physiology\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6">\n         <a href="#Taxonomy">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Taxonomy\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7">\n         <a href="#Genomes_and_genome_sequencing">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Genomes and genome sequencing\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8">\n         <a href="#Ecological_importance">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Ecological importance\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Description">\n        Description\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="463" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg/199px-Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg/299px-Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg/398px-Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg 2x" width="199"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze" title="Johann August Ephraim Goeze">\n          Johann August Ephraim Goeze\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:201px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spallanzani.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1043" data-file-width="817" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Spallanzani.jpg/199px-Spallanzani.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Spallanzani.jpg/299px-Spallanzani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Spallanzani.jpg/398px-Spallanzani.jpg 2x" width="199"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spallanzani.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Lazzaro_Spallanzani" title="Lazzaro Spallanzani">\n          Lazzaro Spallanzani\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Johann_August_Ephraim_Goeze" title="Johann August Ephraim Goeze">\n        Johann August Ephraim Goeze\n       </a>\n       originally named the tardigrade\n       <i>\n        kleiner Wasserb\xc3\xa4r\n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        B\xc3\xa4rtierchen\n       </i>\n       today), meaning "little water bear" in German. The name\n       <i>\n        Tardigradum\n       </i>\n       means "slow walker" and was given by\n       <a href="/wiki/Lazzaro_Spallanzani" title="Lazzaro Spallanzani">\n        Lazzaro Spallanzani\n       </a>\n       in 1776.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bordenstein-2008_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Bordenstein-2008-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The name \'water bear\' comes from the way they walk, reminiscent of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bear" title="Bear">\n        bear\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Gait" title="Gait">\n        gait\n       </a>\n       . The biggest adults may reach a body length of 1.5\xc2\xa0mm (0.059\xc2\xa0in), the smallest below 0.1\xc2\xa0mm. Newly hatched tardigrades may be smaller than 0.05\xc2\xa0mm.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Waterbear.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="266" data-file-width="266" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Waterbear.jpg/220px-Waterbear.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Waterbear.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Waterbear.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         SEM image of\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Hypsibius_dujardini" title="Hypsibius dujardini">\n           Hypsibius dujardini\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The most convenient place to find tardigrades is on lichens and mosses. Other environments are\n       <a href="/wiki/Dune" title="Dune">\n        dunes\n       </a>\n       , beaches,\n       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">\n        soil\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">\n        marine\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">\n        freshwater\n       </a>\n       sediments, where they may occur quite frequently (up to 25,000 animals per liter). Tardigrades, in the case of\n       <i>\n        Echiniscoides wyethi\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-20150929_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AP-20150929-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       may be found on\n       <a href="/wiki/Barnacle" title="Barnacle">\n        barnacles\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBSW_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PBSW-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Often, tardigrades can be found by soaking a piece of moss in water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Anatomy_and_morphology">\n        Anatomy and morphology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Anatomy and morphology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades have barrel-shaped bodies with four pairs of stubby legs. Most range from 0.3 to 0.5\xc2\xa0mm (0.012 to 0.020\xc2\xa0in) in length, although the largest species may reach 1.2\xc2\xa0mm (0.047\xc2\xa0in). The body consists of a head, three body\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segment_(biology)" title="Segment (biology)">\n        segments\n       </a>\n       with a pair of legs each, and a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caudal_(anatomical_term)#Anterior_and_posterior" title="Caudal (anatomical term)">\n        caudal\n       </a>\n       segment with a fourth pair of legs. The legs are without\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_(anatomy)" title="Joint (anatomy)">\n        joints\n       </a>\n       , while the feet have four to eight claws each. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuticle" title="Cuticle">\n        cuticle\n       </a>\n       contains\n       <a href="/wiki/Chitin" title="Chitin">\n        chitin\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Protein" title="Protein">\n        protein\n       </a>\n       and is\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecdysis" title="Ecdysis">\n        moulted\n       </a>\n       periodically.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All adult tardigrades of the same species have the same number of cells (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Eutely" title="Eutely">\n        eutely\n       </a>\n       ). Some species have as many as 40,000 cells in each adult, while others have far fewer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seki98_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Seki98-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The body cavity consists of a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haemocoel" title="Haemocoel">\n        haemocoel\n       </a>\n       , but the only place where a true\n       <a href="/wiki/Coelom" title="Coelom">\n        coelom\n       </a>\n       can be found is around the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gonad" title="Gonad">\n        gonad\n       </a>\n       . No respiratory organs are found, with gas exchange able to occur across the whole of the body. Some tardigrades have three tubular glands associated with the rectum; these may be excretory organs similar to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malpighian_tubule" title="Malpighian tubule">\n        Malpighian tubules\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">\n        arthropods\n       </a>\n       , although the details remain unclear.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IZ_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IZ-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The tubular mouth is armed with\n       <a href="/wiki/Stylet_(anatomy)" title="Stylet (anatomy)">\n        stylets\n       </a>\n       , which are used to pierce the plant cells,\n       <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">\n        algae\n       </a>\n       , or small invertebrates on which the tardigrades feed, releasing the body fluids or cell contents. The mouth opens into a triradiate, muscular, sucking\n       <a href="/wiki/Pharynx" title="Pharynx">\n        pharynx\n       </a>\n       . The stylets are lost when the animal\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molting" title="Molting">\n        molts\n       </a>\n       , and a new pair is secreted from a pair of glands that lie on either side of the mouth. The pharynx connects to a short\n       <a href="/wiki/Esophagus" title="Esophagus">\n        esophagus\n       </a>\n       , and then to an intestine that occupies much of the length of the body, which is the main site of digestion. The intestine opens, via a short rectum, to an\n       <a href="/wiki/Anus" title="Anus">\n        anus\n       </a>\n       located at the terminal end of the body. Some species only defecate when they molt, leaving the feces behind with the shed cuticle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IZ_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IZ-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The brain develops in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Symmetry_in_biology#Bilateral_symmetry" title="Symmetry in biology">\n        bilaterally symmetric\n       </a>\n       pattern.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid26052416_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pmid26052416-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The brain includes multiple lobes, mostly consisting of three bilaterally paired clusters of\n       <a href="/wiki/Neuron" title="Neuron">\n        neurons\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The brain is attached to a large\n       <a href="/wiki/Ganglion" title="Ganglion">\n        ganglion\n       </a>\n       below the esophagus, from which a double\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ventral_nervous_system" title="Ventral nervous system">\n        ventral nerve cord\n       </a>\n       runs the length of the body. The cord possesses one ganglion per segment, each of which produces lateral nerve fibres that run into the limbs. Many species possess a pair of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhabdomeric" title="Rhabdomeric">\n        rhabdomeric\n       </a>\n       pigment-cup eyes, and numerous sensory bristles are on the head and body.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greven2007_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Greven2007-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades all possess a\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/buccopharyngeal" title="wikt:buccopharyngeal">\n        buccopharyngeal\n       </a>\n       apparatus (swallowing device made of muscles and spines that acts an inner jaw and begins digestion and movement along the throat and intestine\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ) which, along with the claws, is used to differentiate among species.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reproduction">\n        Reproduction\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reproduction">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg/200px-TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg/300px-TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg/400px-TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TardigradeEggsInShedCuticle.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Shed cuticle of female tardigrade, containing eggs.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Although some species are\n       <a href="/wiki/Parthenogenesis" title="Parthenogenesis">\n        parthenogenic\n       </a>\n       , both males and females are usually present, each with a single\n       <a href="/wiki/Gonad" title="Gonad">\n        gonad\n       </a>\n       located above the intestine. Two ducts run from the testis in males, opening through a single pore in front of the anus. In contrast, females have a single duct opening either just above the anus or directly into the rectum, which thus forms a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cloaca" title="Cloaca">\n        cloaca\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IZ_31-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IZ-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oviparous" title="Oviparous">\n        oviparous\n       </a>\n       , and fertilization is usually external. Mating occurs during the molt with the eggs being laid inside the shed\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuticle" title="Cuticle">\n        cuticle\n       </a>\n       of the female and then covered with sperm. A few species have internal fertilization, with mating occurring before the female fully sheds her cuticle. In most cases, the eggs are left inside the shed cuticle to develop, but some species attach them to nearby substrate.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IZ_31-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IZ-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The eggs hatch after no more than 14 days, with the young already possessing their full complement of adult\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_(biology)" title="Cell (biology)">\n        cells\n       </a>\n       . Growth to the adult size therefore occurs by enlargement of the individual cells (\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypertrophy" title="Hypertrophy">\n        hypertrophy\n       </a>\n       ), rather than by cell division. Tardigrades may molt up to 12 times.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IZ_31-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-IZ-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology_and_life_history">\n        Ecology and life history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecology and life history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">\n          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          <b>\n           This section needs expansion\n          </b>\n          .\n          <small>\n           You can help by\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">\n            adding to it\n           </a>\n           .\n          </small>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (November 2014)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Most tardigrades are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phytophagous" title="Phytophagous">\n        phytophagous\n       </a>\n       (plant eaters) or\n       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/bacteriophagous" title="wikt:bacteriophagous">\n        bacteriophagous\n       </a>\n       (bacteria eaters), but some are\n       <a href="/wiki/Carnivore" title="Carnivore">\n        carnivorous\n       </a>\n       to the extent of eating other smaller species of tardigrades (e.g.,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Milnesium_tardigradum" title="Milnesium tardigradum">\n         Milnesium tardigradum\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades share morphological characteristics with many species that differ largely by class. Biologists have a difficult time finding verification among tardigrade species because of this relationship. These animals are most closely related to the early evolution of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">\n        arthropods\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrade fossils go as far back as the Cretaceous period in North America. This specific species is considered cosmopolitan and can be located in regions all over the world. The eggs and cysts of tardigrades are so resistant to other dangers that they are carried great distances, on the feet of other animals, to a different location.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physiology">\n        Physiology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Physiology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hypsibiusdujardini.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="237" data-file-width="288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Hypsibiusdujardini.jpg/200px-Hypsibiusdujardini.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Hypsibiusdujardini.jpg 1.5x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hypsibiusdujardini.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Hypsibius_dujardini" title="Hypsibius dujardini">\n           Hypsibius dujardini\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         imaged with a\n         <a href="/wiki/Scanning_electron_microscope" title="Scanning electron microscope">\n          scanning electron microscope\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Scientists have reported tardigrades in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">\n        hot springs\n       </a>\n       , on top of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">\n        Himalayas\n       </a>\n       , under layers of solid\n       <a href="/wiki/Ice" title="Ice">\n        ice\n       </a>\n       , and in ocean sediments. Many species can be found in milder environments such as lakes, ponds, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Meadow" title="Meadow">\n        meadows\n       </a>\n       , while others can be found in stone walls and roofs. Tardigrades are most common in moist environments, but can stay active wherever they can retain at least some moisture.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades are one of the few groups of species that are capable of suspending their metabolism (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Cryptobiosis" title="Cryptobiosis">\n        cryptobiosis\n       </a>\n       ). Many species of tardigrade can survive in a dehydrated state up to five years, or in exceptional cases longer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Depending on the environment, they may enter this state via\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anhydrobiosis" title="Anhydrobiosis">\n        anhydrobiosis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryobiosis" title="Cryobiosis">\n        cryobiosis\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Osmobiosis" title="Osmobiosis">\n        osmobiosis\n       </a>\n       , or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anoxybiosis" title="Anoxybiosis">\n        anoxybiosis\n       </a>\n       . While in this state, their metabolism lowers to less than 0.01% of normal and their water content can drop to 1% of normal.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20150907_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NYT-20150907-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Their ability to remain desiccated for such long periods was thought to be largely dependent on the high levels of the nonreducing sugar\n       <a href="/wiki/Trehalose" title="Trehalose">\n        trehalose\n       </a>\n       , which protects their\n       <a href="/wiki/Cell_membrane" title="Cell membrane">\n        membranes\n       </a>\n       , though recent research suggests that tardigrades have a unique type of\n       <a href="/wiki/Intrinsically_disordered_proteins" title="Intrinsically disordered proteins">\n        disordered protein\n       </a>\n       that serves a similar purpose: It replaces water in the cells and adopts a glassy, vitrified state when the animals dry out.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Their DNA is further protected from radiation by a protein called "\n       <a href="/wiki/Dsup" title="Dsup">\n        dsup\n       </a>\n       " (short for\n       <i>\n        damage suppressor\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hashimoto_et_al._2015_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hashimoto_et_al._2015-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In this cryptobiotic state, the tardigrade is known as a tun.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrades are able to survive in extreme environments that would kill almost any other animal. Extremes at which tardigrades can survive include those of:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">\n         Temperature\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 tardigrades can survive:\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          A few minutes at 151\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (304\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F)\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survival_46-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-survival-46">\n            [46]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          30 years at \xe2\x88\x9220\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x924\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F)\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CB-201602_47-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-CB-201602-47">\n            [47]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          A few days at \xe2\x88\x92200\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x92328\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F)\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-survival_46-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-survival-46">\n            [46]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          A few minutes at \xe2\x88\x92272\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (\xe2\x88\x92458\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F; 1\xc2\xa0K)\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n           <a href="#cite_note-48">\n            [48]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">\n         Pressure\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 they can withstand the extremely low pressure of a\n        <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">\n         vacuum\n        </a>\n        and also very high pressures, more than 1,200 times\n        <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">\n         atmospheric pressure\n        </a>\n        . Tardigrades can survive the vacuum of open space and solar radiation combined for at least 10 days.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-low-earth-orbit_49-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-low-earth-orbit-49">\n          [49]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Some species can also withstand pressure of 6,000 atmospheres, which is nearly six times the pressure of water in the deepest ocean trench, the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mariana_trench" title="Mariana trench">\n         Mariana trench\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Seki98_29-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Seki98-29">\n          [29]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dehydration" title="Dehydration">\n         Dehydration\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 the longest that living tardigrades have been shown to survive in a dry state is nearly 10 years,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_15-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-auto-15">\n          [15]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guidetti.2C_R._.26_J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K.I._2002_181.E2.80.93187_16-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Guidetti.2C_R._.26_J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K.I._2002_181.E2.80.93187-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        although there is one report of leg movement, not generally considered "survival",\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K._Ingemar_.26_R._Bertolani_2001_121.E2.80.93123_50-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K._Ingemar_.26_R._Bertolani_2001_121.E2.80.93123-50">\n          [50]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        in a 120-year-old specimen from dried moss.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franceschi.2C_T._1948_47.E2.80.9349_51-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Franceschi.2C_T._1948_47.E2.80.9349-51">\n          [51]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        When exposed to extremely low temperatures, their body composition goes from 85% water to only 3%. As water expands upon freezing, dehydration ensures the tardigrades do not get ripped apart by the freezing ice.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n         <a href="#cite_note-52">\n          [52]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">\n         Radiation\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 tardigrades can withstand 1,000 times more radiation than other animals,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n         <a href="#cite_note-53">\n          [53]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        median lethal doses of 5,000\n        <a href="/wiki/Gray_(unit)" title="Gray (unit)">\n         Gy\n        </a>\n        (of gamma rays) and 6,200 Gy (of heavy ions) in hydrated animals (5 to 10 Gy could be fatal to a human).\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horikawa_et_al._2006_54-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Horikawa_et_al._2006-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        The only explanation found in earlier experiments for this ability was that their lowered water state provides fewer reactants for\n        <a href="/wiki/Ionizing_radiation" title="Ionizing radiation">\n         ionizing radiation\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horikawa_et_al._2006_54-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Horikawa_et_al._2006-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        However, subsequent research found that tardigrades, when hydrated, still remain highly resistant to shortwave\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV_radiation" title="UV radiation">\n         UV radiation\n        </a>\n        in comparison to other animals, and that one factor for this is their ability to efficiently repair damage to their DNA resulting from that exposure.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n         <a href="#cite_note-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        Irradiation of tardigrade eggs collected directly from a natural substrate (moss) showed a clear dose-related response, with a steep decline in hatchability at doses up to 4\xc2\xa0kGy, above which no eggs hatched.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.C3.B6nsson_2013_56-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-J.C3.B6nsson_2013-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        The eggs were more tolerant to radiation late in development. No eggs irradiated at the early developmental stage hatched, and only one egg at middle stage hatched, while eggs irradiated in the late stage hatched at a rate indistinguishable from controls.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.C3.B6nsson_2013_56-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-J.C3.B6nsson_2013-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Toxicant" title="Toxicant">\n         Environmental toxins\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 tardigrades are reported to undergo chemobiosis, a\n        <a href="/wiki/Cryptobiosis" title="Cryptobiosis">\n         cryptobiotic\n        </a>\n        response to high levels of environmental toxins. However, As of 2001\n        <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit">\n          [update]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        , these laboratory results have yet to be verified.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K._Ingemar_.26_R._Bertolani_2001_121.E2.80.93123_50-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-J.C3.B6nsson.2C_K._Ingemar_.26_R._Bertolani_2001_121.E2.80.93123-50">\n          [50]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Franceschi.2C_T._1948_47.E2.80.9349_51-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Franceschi.2C_T._1948_47.E2.80.9349-51">\n          [51]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">\n         Outer space\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 tardigrades are the first known animal to survive in space. In September 2007, dehydrated tardigrades were taken into\n        <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n         low Earth orbit\n        </a>\n        on the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foton-M" title="Foton-M">\n         FOTON-M3\n        </a>\n        mission carrying the\n        <a href="/wiki/BIOPAN" title="BIOPAN">\n         BIOPAN\n        </a>\n        astrobiology payload. For 10 days, groups of tardigrades were exposed to the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hard_vacuum" title="Hard vacuum">\n         hard vacuum\n        </a>\n        of outer space, or vacuum and solar\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV" title="UV">\n         UV\n        </a>\n        radiation.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WRD-20140321_3-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-WRD-20140321-3">\n          [3]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Science-20080908_57-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Science-20080908-57">\n          [57]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MSNBC-20111222_58-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-MSNBC-20111222-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        After being rehydrated back on Earth, over 68% of the subjects protected from high-energy UV radiation revived within 30 minutes following rehydration, but subsequent mortality was high; many of these produced viable embryos.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-low-earth-orbit_49-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-low-earth-orbit-49">\n          [49]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n         <a href="#cite_note-59">\n          [59]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In contrast, hydrated samples exposed to the combined effect of vacuum and full solar UV radiation had significantly reduced survival, with only three subjects of\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Milnesium_tardigradum" title="Milnesium tardigradum">\n          Milnesium tardigradum\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        surviving.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-low-earth-orbit_49-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-low-earth-orbit-49">\n          [49]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In May 2011, Italian scientists sent tardigrades on board the International Space Station along with extremophiles on\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n         STS-134\n        </a>\n        , the final flight of\n        <span class="nowrap">\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n          Space Shuttle\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n         <a href="#cite_note-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n         <a href="#cite_note-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n         <a href="#cite_note-62">\n          [62]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Their conclusion was that microgravity and cosmic radiation "did not significantly affect survival of tardigrades in flight, confirming that tardigrades represent a useful animal for space research."\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n         <a href="#cite_note-63">\n          [63]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        In November 2011, they were among the organisms to be sent by the U.S.-based\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planetary_Society" title="Planetary Society">\n         Planetary Society\n        </a>\n        on the Russian\n        <a href="/wiki/Fobos-Grunt" title="Fobos-Grunt">\n         Fobos-Grunt\n        </a>\n        mission\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/Living_Interplanetary_Flight_Experiment" title="Living Interplanetary Flight Experiment">\n         Living Interplanetary Flight Experiment\n        </a>\n        to\n        <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">\n         Phobos\n        </a>\n        ; however, the launch failed. Tardigrades are one of the few groups to have survived Earth\'s five\n        <a href="/wiki/Extinction_event" title="Extinction event">\n         mass extinctions\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n         <a href="#cite_note-64">\n          [64]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxonomy">\n        Taxonomy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Taxonomy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_bilaterial_animal_orders" title="List of bilaterial animal orders">\n        List of bilaterial animal orders\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Echiniscus_sp.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="528" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Echiniscus_sp.jpg/200px-Echiniscus_sp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Echiniscus_sp.jpg/300px-Echiniscus_sp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Echiniscus_sp.jpg/400px-Echiniscus_sp.jpg 2x" width="200"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Echiniscus_sp.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Illustration of\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Echiniscus" title="Echiniscus">\n           Echiniscus\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         sp. from 1861\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Scientists have conducted\n       <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">\n        morphological\n       </a>\n       and molecular studies to understand how tardigrades relate to other lineages of ecdysozoan animals. Two plausible placements have been proposed: tardigrades are either most closely related to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthropoda" title="Arthropoda">\n        Arthropoda\n       </a>\n       \xc2\xb1\n       <a href="/wiki/Onychophora" title="Onychophora">\n        Onychophora\n       </a>\n       , or tardigrades are most closely related to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nematodes" title="Nematodes">\n        nematodes\n       </a>\n       . Evidence for the former is a common result of\n       <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(biology)" title="Morphology (biology)">\n        morphological studies\n       </a>\n       ; evidence of the latter is found in some molecular analyses.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The latter hypothesis has been rejected by recent\n       <a href="/wiki/MicroRNA" title="MicroRNA">\n        microRNA\n       </a>\n       and expressed sequence tag analyses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cambell_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cambell-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Apparently, the grouping of tardigrades with nematodes found in a number of molecular studies is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Long_branch_attraction" title="Long branch attraction">\n        long branch attraction\n       </a>\n       artifact. Within the arthropod group (called panarthropoda and comprising onychophora, tardigrades and euarthropoda), three patterns of relationship are possible: tardigrades sister to\n       <a href="/wiki/Onychophora" title="Onychophora">\n        onychophora\n       </a>\n       plus arthropods (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lobopodia" title="Lobopodia">\n        lobopodia\n       </a>\n       hypothesis); onychophora sister to tardigrades plus arthropods (the tactopoda hypothesis); and onychophora sister to tardigrades.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telford_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Telford-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Recent analyses indicate that the panarthropoda group is monophyletic, and that tardigrades are a sister group of Lobopodia, the lineage consisting of\n       <a href="/wiki/Arthropod" title="Arthropod">\n        arthropods\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Onychophora" title="Onychophora">\n        Onychophora\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cambell_65-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cambell-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table style="border-collapse:collapse;border-spacing:0;margin:0;">\n       <tr>\n        <td style="width:1em;border:0;padding:0 0.2em;border-bottom:1px solid;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Panarthropoda" title="Panarthropoda">\n          Panarthropoda\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td rowspan="2" style="border:0;padding:0;">\n         <table style="border-collapse:collapse;border-spacing:0;margin:0;">\n          <tr>\n           <td style="width:1em;border:0;padding:0 0.2em;border-bottom:1px solid;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;">\n            <br/>\n           </td>\n           <td rowspan="2" style="border:0;padding:0;">\n            <p>\n             <span class="nowrap">\n              Water bears (Tardigrada)\n             </span>\n            </p>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td style="border:0;border-left:1px solid;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;">\n            <br/>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td style="border:0;padding:0 0.2em;border-left:1px solid;border-bottom:1px solid;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;">\n            <a href="/wiki/Lobopodia" title="Lobopodia">\n             Lobopodia\n            </a>\n           </td>\n           <td rowspan="2" style="border:0;padding:0;">\n            <table style="border-collapse:collapse;border-spacing:0;margin:0;">\n             <tr>\n              <td style="width:1em;border:0;padding:0 0.2em;border-bottom:1px solid;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;">\n               <br/>\n              </td>\n              <td rowspan="2" style="border:0;padding:0;">\n               <p>\n                Velvet worms (\n                <a href="/wiki/Onychophora" title="Onychophora">\n                 Onychophora\n                </a>\n                )\n               </p>\n              </td>\n             </tr>\n             <tr>\n              <td style="border:0;border-left:1px solid;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;">\n               <br/>\n              </td>\n             </tr>\n             <tr>\n              <td style="border:0;padding:0 0.2em;border-left:1px solid;border-bottom:1px solid;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;">\n               <br/>\n              </td>\n              <td rowspan="2" style="border:0;padding:0;">\n               <p>\n                Arthropods (\n                <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthropoda" title="Arthropoda">\n                 Arthropoda\n                </a>\n                )\n               </p>\n              </td>\n             </tr>\n             <tr>\n              <td style="border:0;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;">\n               <br/>\n              </td>\n             </tr>\n            </table>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td style="border:0;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;">\n            <br/>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="border:0;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;">\n         <br/>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The minute sizes of tardigrades and their membranous integuments make their\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fossilization" title="Fossilization">\n        fossilization\n       </a>\n       both difficult to detect and highly unusual. The only known fossil specimens are those from mid-\n       <a href="/wiki/Cambrian" title="Cambrian">\n        Cambrian\n       </a>\n       deposits in\n       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">\n        Siberia\n       </a>\n       and a few rare specimens from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">\n        Cretaceous\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">\n        amber\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EotI_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EotI-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Echiniscus_L.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="90" data-file-width="120" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/Echiniscus_L.png" width="120"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Echiniscus_L.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Echiniscus_testudo" title="Echiniscus testudo">\n           Echiniscus testudo\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n          [\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n            <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">\n             citation needed\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          ]\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Siberian tardigrade fossils differ from living tardigrades in several ways. They have three pairs of legs rather than four, they have a simplified head morphology, and they have no posterior head appendages, but they share with modern tardigrades their columnar cuticle construction.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Budd2001_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Budd2001-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Scientists think they represent a stem group of living tardigrades.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EotI_68-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EotI-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rare specimens in Cretaceous amber have been found in two North American locations.\n       <i>\n        Milnesium swolenskyi\n       </i>\n       , from\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">\n        New Jersey\n       </a>\n       , is the older of the two; its claws and mouthparts are indistinguishable from the living\n       <i>\n        M. tardigradum\n       </i>\n       . The other specimens from amber are from western\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       , some 15\xe2\x80\x9320\xc2\xa0million years earlier than\n       <i>\n        M. swolenskyi\n       </i>\n       . One of the two specimens from Canada has been given its own genus and family,\n       <i>\n        Beorn leggi\n       </i>\n       (the genus named by Cooper after the character\n       <a href="/wiki/Beorn" title="Beorn">\n        Beorn\n       </a>\n       from\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">\n         The Hobbit\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       by\n       <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">\n        J. R. R. Tolkien\n       </a>\n       and the species named after his student William M. Legg); however, it bears a strong resemblance to many living specimens in the family\n       <a href="/wiki/Hypsibiidae" title="Hypsibiidae">\n        Hypsibiidae\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EotI_68-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-EotI-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Aysheaia" title="Aysheaia">\n         Aysheaia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       from the middle Cambrian\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burgess_shale" title="Burgess shale">\n        Burgess shale\n       </a>\n       has been proposed as a sister taxon to an arthropod-tardigrade clade.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ArtRels_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ArtRels-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrades have been proposed to be among the closest living relatives of the Burgess shale oddity\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Opabinia" title="Opabinia">\n         Opabinia\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Budd1996_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Budd1996-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Genomes_and_genome_sequencing">\n        Genomes and genome sequencing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Genomes and genome sequencing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Tardigrade\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genomes" title="Genomes">\n        genomes\n       </a>\n       vary in size, from about 75 to 800 megabase pairs of DNA.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Hypsibius dujardini\n       </i>\n       has a compact genome and a generation time of about two weeks; it can be cultured indefinitely and cryopreserved.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The genome of\n       <i>\n        Ramazzottius varieornatus,\n       </i>\n       one of the most stress-tolerant species of Tardigrades, was sequenced by a team of researchers from the University of Tokyo in 2015. Analysis revealed less than 1.2% of its genes were the result of\n       <a href="/wiki/Horizontal_gene_transfer" title="Horizontal gene transfer">\n        horizontal gene transfer\n       </a>\n       . They also found evidence of a loss of gene pathways that are known to promote damage due to stress. This study also found a high expression of novel Tardigrade-unique proteins, including Damage suppressor (Dsup), which was shown to protect against DNA damage from X-ray radiation. The same team applied the Dsup protein to human cultured cells and found that it suppressed X-ray damage to the human cells by ~40%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hashimoto_et_al._2015_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Hashimoto_et_al._2015-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecological_importance">\n        Ecological importance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ecological importance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Many organisms that live in aquatic environments feed on species such as nematodes, tardigrades, bacteria, algae, mites, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collembolan" title="Collembolan">\n        collembolans\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Tardigrades work as pioneer species by inhabiting new developing environments in which to live. This movement attracts other invertebrates to populate that space, while also attracting predators.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tardigrade&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n      Antarctica\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
